 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;2.02. Results of Operations and Financial Condition. </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;31, 2018, we issued a press release announcing earnings for the fourth quarter and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. A copy of the earnings
press release is furnished as Exhibit 99.1 to this current report. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This information, including Exhibit 99.1, will not be deemed &#147;filed&#148; for
purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;), or otherwise subject to the liabilities under that section and it will not be incorporated by reference in any filing under the Securities
Act of 1933, as amended, or the Exchange Act, except as expressly set forth by specific reference in such a filing. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Item&nbsp;8.01. Other Events.
</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On January&nbsp;31, 2018, our Finance Committee, with authorization from our Board of Directors, approved an increase of $6.0 billion in our share
repurchase program and an extension of the expiration date of the program. We are now authorized to repurchase up to $19.7 billion of our Class&nbsp;A Common Stock through December&nbsp;31, 2020, up from the previous authorization of $13.7 billion.
We may repurchase the shares in one or more open market transactions, privately negotiated transactions or a combination of the foregoing. </P>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Returned $3.4&nbsp;billion in capital to shareholders </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">DEERFIELD, Ill. &#150; Jan. 31, 2018
&#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported its fourth quarter and full-year 2017 results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We are
pleased with the solid results for 2017,&#148; said Brian Gladden, Chief Financial Officer. &#147;We delivered a strong year of margin expansion and earnings growth, marking significant progress from four years ago. Our improved <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-line</FONT> performance was fueled by our Power Brands and favorable trends in emerging markets.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;I&#146;m very excited about the opportunities ahead to create value at Mondel&#275;z International,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chief
Executive Officer.&nbsp;&#147;We have strong foundational pillars in place, and we enter the year with improving momentum in our business. Our 2018 plan reflects an emphasis on execution, ongoing improvements in
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-line</FONT> growth and continuing actions to expand margins. As we develop our long-term strategic plan for sustainable growth, we&#146;re focused on how we can optimize and accelerate our strengths to create
more moments of joy for our consumers, customers, communities, colleagues and shareholders.&#148; </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">1 </P>

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">2 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Fourth Quarter Commentary </I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 2.9&nbsp;percent, driven by currency and Organic Net Revenue growth partly offset by divestiture impacts. <B>Organic Net Revenue</B> increased 2.4&nbsp;percent, which includes a positive
impact of approximately 60 basis points from India demonetization in the prior year. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Gross profit margin</B> was 38.2&nbsp;percent, flat to the prior year, as favorable impacts from commodity hedging activities and divestitures were offset by incremental costs due to the malware incident and higher
2014-2018 Restructuring Program implementation costs. <B>Adjusted Gross Profit</B><B><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP></B><B> margin</B> was 39.2&nbsp;percent, flat to the prior year, driven by cost inflation and unfavorable
mix, offset by improved pricing and net productivity gains. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Operating income margin</B> was 12.1&nbsp;percent, up 460 basis points, driven by lower 2014-2018 Restructuring Program costs, higher Adjusted Operating Income margin and the lapping of the prior year&#146;s
intangible asset impairment.<B>&nbsp;Adjusted Operating Income margin</B> expanded 180 basis points to 15.9&nbsp;percent. These results reflected reductions in selling, general&nbsp;&amp; administrative costs and supply chain productivity savings.
</TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.53, up 783&nbsp;percent, driven by the lapping of the prior year loss on debt extinguishment, lower intangible asset impairment costs and a net benefit from U.S. tax reform. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $0.57 and grew 21&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by operating gains. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company repurchased approximately $400&nbsp;million of its common stock and paid approximately $300&nbsp;million in cash dividends. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Tax Rate: </B>The enactment of U.S. tax reform in December 2017 resulted in a discrete net tax benefit of $59&nbsp;million in the fourth quarter. Elements of this benefit include a tax on the company&#146;s
accumulated foreign earnings (estimated $1.3&nbsp;billion cost) and the revaluation of its net U.S. deferred tax liability (estimated $1.3&nbsp;billion benefit). As a result, the company&#146;s reported effective tax rate, which includes these
discrete tax impacts, was 24.6&nbsp;percent for the fourth quarter and 22.0&nbsp;percent for the full year. The company&#146;s Adjusted Effective Tax Rate<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP>, which excludes the discrete net tax
impacts, was 24.5&nbsp;percent for the fourth quarter and 22.8&nbsp;percent for the full year. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Full-Year Commentary </I></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Net revenues</B> decreased 0.1&nbsp;percent, driven by divestitures that offset Organic Net Revenue growth and currency tailwinds. <B>Organic Net Revenue</B> increased 0.9&nbsp;percent, which included a negative
impact of approximately 40 basis points from the June malware incident. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Gross profit margin</B> was 38.9&nbsp;percent, a decrease of 20 basis points, driven primarily by Adjusted Gross Profit margin contraction and the impact from the malware incident costs, partially offset by lower
2014-2018 Restructuring Program implementation costs and lower <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts. <B>Adjusted Gross Profit
margin</B> was 39.8&nbsp;percent, a decrease of 30 basis points. Higher input costs and unfavorable volume/mix more than offset net productivity gains and improved pricing net of select trade investments. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Operating income margin</B><B></B>&nbsp;was 13.5&nbsp;percent,&nbsp;up 360 basis points, driven by Adjusted Operating Income margin expansion, lower 2014-2018 Restructuring Program costs, benefits from the resolution
of tax matters and a net gain on divestitures, partially offset by malware incident incremental expenses.<B>&nbsp;Adjusted Operating Income margin</B> expanded 130 basis points to 16.3&nbsp;percent. These results reflected supply chain productivity
savings and reductions in overhead costs. </TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">3 </P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $1.91, up 82&nbsp;percent, driven by the lapping of the prior year loss on debt extinguishment, benefits from the resolution of tax matters, lower 2014-2018 Restructuring Program costs, net gains
from divestitures and a net benefit from U.S. tax reform. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $2.14 and grew 15&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by operating gains, lower interest expense and lower shares outstanding. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company returned $3.4&nbsp;billion of capital to shareholders through share repurchases and dividends. Today, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a $6&nbsp;billion increase to the
company&#146;s share repurchase authorization from $13.7&nbsp;billion to $19.7&nbsp;billion and extended the expiration date of the program to December&nbsp;31, 2020. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2018 Outlook </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International
provides guidance on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> basis, as the company cannot predict some elements that are included in reported GAAP results, including the impact of foreign exchange. Refer to the Outlook section in the
discussion of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures below for more details. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For 2018, the company expects
Organic Net Revenue to increase 1 to 2&nbsp;percent. The company expects Adjusted Operating Income margin of approximately 17&nbsp;percent. The company also expects double-digit Adjusted EPS growth on a constant-currency basis. This 2018 outlook
includes an expected Adjusted Effective Tax Rate in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">low-to-mid</FONT></FONT> 20&nbsp;percent range, including our current view of the expected impact of U.S. tax reform. The
company estimates currency translation would increase net revenue growth by approximately 4 percent<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP> and Adjusted EPS by approximately $0.12<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP>.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z
International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on
the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) is building the best snacking company in the world, with 2017 net revenues of approximately
$26&nbsp;billion. Creating more moments of joy in approximately 160 countries, Mondel&#275;z International is a world leader in biscuits, chocolate, gum, candy and powdered beverages, featuring global Power Brands such as <I>Oreo </I>and<I> belVita
</I>biscuits<I>; Cadbury Dairy Milk</I> and <I>Milka</I> chocolate; and <I>Trident</I> gum.&nbsp;Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit<U>
www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>

</B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Power Brands include some of the company&#146;s largest global and regional brands, such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>Chips Ahoy!</I>, <I>Ritz,
TUC/Club Social</I> and <I>belVita</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk, Milka</I> and <I>Lacta</I> chocolate; <I>Trident</I> gum; <I>Halls</I> candy; and <I>Tang</I> powdered beverages. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand
and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Belarus, Georgia, Poland, Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets include the entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets
definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region.</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking Statements </B></P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business. Management
uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these measures allows
investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments
generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities,
constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial
measures included herein. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to
be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or
comparable to similar <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Because GAAP financial measures on a
forward-looking basis are not accessible and reconciling information is not available without unreasonable effort, the company has not provided that information with regard to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
in the company&#146;s outlook. Refer to the Outlook section below for more details. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">10 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its
operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the
related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(1)</SUP>. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148; is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions; divestitures <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical global coffee business <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>; the historical Venezuelan operations; accounting calendar changes; and currency rate fluctuations <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. The company believes that Organic Net
Revenue reflects the underlying growth from the ongoing activities of its business and provides improved comparability of results. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and its Power Brands. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148; is defined as gross profit excluding the 2012-2014 Restructuring Program <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; acquisition integration costs; incremental costs associated with the Jacobs Douwe Egberts (&#147;JDE&#148;) coffee business transactions; the operating results of divestitures <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical coffee business operating results <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>; the historical Venezuelan operating results; and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(6)</SUP>. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit
margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company believes that Adjusted Gross Profit and Adjusted Gross Profit margin provide improved comparability of underlying operating results. The company also
evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148; are defined as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the 2012-2014 Restructuring Program <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; Venezuela remeasurement and deconsolidation losses and historical operating results; gains or losses
(including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>&nbsp;or acquisition gains or losses and related integration and
acquisition costs; the JDE coffee business transactions <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top"></SUP>&nbsp;gain and net incremental costs; the operating results of divestitures <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; the historical global coffee business operating results <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP>;
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(6)</SUP>; equity method
investment earnings historically reported within operating income <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(7)</SUP>; benefits from resolution of tax matters <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(8)</SUP>; CEO transition remuneration
<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(9)</SUP>; and incremental expenses related to the malware incident. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income margin&#148;,
which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company believes that Adjusted Operating Income, Adjusted Segment Operating Income, Adjusted Operating Income margin and Adjusted
Segment Operating Income margin provide improved comparability of underlying operating results. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a constant currency basis <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Adjusted EPS&#148; is defined as diluted EPS attributable to Mondel&#275;z International from continuing operations excluding the impacts of the 2012-2014 Restructuring Program <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(5)</SUP>; Venezuela remeasurement and deconsolidation losses and historical operating results; losses on debt
extinguishment and related expenses; gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>&nbsp;or
acquisition gains or losses and related integration and acquisition costs; the JDE coffee business transactions <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(3)</SUP><SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top"></SUP>&nbsp;gain, transaction
hedging gains or losses and net incremental costs; gain on equity method investment transactions; net earnings from divestitures <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(2)</SUP>; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(6)</SUP>; gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer
designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; benefits from resolution of tax matters <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(8)</SUP>; CEO transition remuneration <SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(9)</SUP>; incremental expenses related to the malware incident; and U.S. tax reform discrete impacts <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(10)</SUP>. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the
company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(11)</SUP>. The tax impact of each of the items excluded from the
company&#146;s GAAP results was computed based on the facts and tax assumptions associated with each item and such impacts have also been excluded from Adjusted EPS. The company believes that Adjusted EPS provides improved comparability of
underlying operating results. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted EPS on a constant currency basis <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(4)</SUP>. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">&#147;Free Cash Flow&#148; is defined as net cash provided by operating activities less capital expenditures. As Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance, the
company believes this <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure provides investors additional useful information when evaluating its cash from operating activities. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. During 2017, the company added to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions the exclusion of: benefits from the resolution of tax matters (see footnote (8)&nbsp;below),
CEO transition remuneration (see footnote (9)&nbsp;below), incremental expenses related to the malware incident and U.S. tax reform discrete items (see footnote (10)&nbsp;below). </TD></TR></TABLE>

<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:8pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The company continues to have an ongoing interest in the legacy coffee business it deconsolidated in 2015 as part of the JDE coffee business transactions. For historical periods prior to the July&nbsp;15, 2015 coffee
business deconsolidation, the company has reclassified any net revenue or operating income from the historical coffee business and included them where the coffee equity method investment earnings are presented within Adjusted EPS. As such, Organic
Net Revenue, Adjusted Gross Profit and Adjusted Operating Income in all periods do not include the results of the company&#146;s legacy coffee businesses, which are shown within Adjusted EPS only. </TD></TR></TABLE>

statements in the comparable prior-year period to determine what the current-period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

chain network and organizational structure. Costs that do not meet the program objectives are not reflected in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> adjustments. Refer to the company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016 for more information on the 2012-2014 Restructuring Program. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="8%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(6)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">During the third quarter of 2016, the company began to exclude unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding
commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. Since the company purchases commodity and
forecasted currency contracts to mitigate price volatility primarily for inventory requirements in future periods, the company made this adjustment to remove the volatility of these future inventory purchases on current operating results to
facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating performance across periods. The company also discontinued designating commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives for hedge accounting treatment. To facilitate comparisons of the
company&#146;s underlying operating results, the company has recast all historical <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures to exclude the
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="8%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(7)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">Historically, the company has recorded income from equity method investments within its operating income as these investments operated as extensions of the company&#146;s base business. Beginning in the third quarter of
2015, the company began to record the earnings from its equity method investments in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> equity method investment earnings outside of operating income following the deconsolidation of its coffee
business. Refer to Note 1, <I>Summary of Significant Accounting Policies</I>, in the company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016 for more information. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">On November&nbsp;20, 2017, Dirk Van de Put succeeded Irene Rosenfeld as CEO of Mondel&#275;z International in advance of her retirement at the end of March 2018. In order to incent Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put to join the
company, the company provided him compensation with a total combined target value of $42.5&nbsp;million to make him whole for incentive awards he forfeited or grants that were not made to him when he left his former employer. The compensation the
company granted took the form of cash, deferred stock units, performance share units and stock options. In connection with Irene Rosenfeld&#146;s retirement, the company made her outstanding grants of performance share units for the 2016-2018 and
2017-2019 performance cycles eligible for continued vesting and approved a $0.5&nbsp;million salary for her service as Chairman from January through March 2018. The company refers to these elements of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and
Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s compensation arrangements together as &#147;CEO transition remuneration.&#148; The company is excluding amounts it expenses as CEO transition remuneration from its 2017 and future
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts are not part of the company&#146;s regular compensation program and are incremental to amounts the company would have incurred as ongoing CEO compensation. As a result,
in 2017, the company excluded amounts expensed for the cash payment to Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put and partial vesting of his equity grants. In 2018, the company expects to exclude amounts paid for Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s service as Chairman and partial
vesting of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s equity grants. </TD></TR></TABLE>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top">The company has excluded its proportionate share of its equity method investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items, such as acquisitions and divestiture related costs, restructuring program costs and discrete U.S. tax
reform impacts, in order to provide investors with a comparable view of its performance across periods. Although the company has shareholder rights and board representation commensurate with its ownership interests in its equity method investees and
reviews the underlying operating results and unusual or infrequent items with them each reporting period, the company does not have direct control over the operations or resulting revenue and expenses. The company&#146;s use of equity method
investment net earnings on an adjusted basis is not intended to imply that the company has any such control. The company&#146;s GAAP &#147;diluted EPS attributable to Mondel&#275;z International from continuing operations&#148; includes all of its
investees&#146; unusual and infrequent items. </TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached schedules for supplemental financial data and corresponding reconciliations
of the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures referred to above to the most comparable GAAP financial measures for the three months and year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment
operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and
losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and
acquisition-related costs, in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages interest and
other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:18pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><B>ITEMS</B></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><B>IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative
and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the
company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures, Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;28, 2017, the company completed the sale of a confectionery business in Japan. The company recorded a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> loss of $1&nbsp;million. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In connection with the 2012 <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">spin-off</FONT> of
Kraft Foods Group, Inc. (now a part of Kraft Heinz Company (&#147;KHC&#148;)), Kraft Foods Group and the company each granted the other various licenses to use certain trademarks in connection with particular product categories in specified
jurisdictions. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the company entered into two agreements with KHC to terminate the licenses of certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">KHC-owned</FONT> brands used in the company&#146;s grocery business within its Europe
region and to transfer to KHC inventory and certain other assets. On August&nbsp;17, 2017, the first transaction closed, and on October&nbsp;23, 2017, the second transaction closed. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;4, 2017, the company completed the sale of most of its grocery business in Australia and New Zealand to Bega Cheese Limited for $456&nbsp;million
Australian dollars ($347&nbsp;million as of July&nbsp;4, 2017). The company recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $247&nbsp;million Australian dollars ($187&nbsp;million as of July&nbsp;4, 2017) on the sale. The company
also recorded divestiture-related costs of $2&nbsp;million and a foreign currency hedge loss of $3&nbsp;million during 2017. In the fourth quarter of 2017, the company recorded a $3&nbsp;million inventory-related working capital adjustment,
increasing the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain to $190&nbsp;million in 2017. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">13 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;28, 2017, the company completed the sale of several manufacturing facilities in France and the sale
or license of several local confectionery brands. The company recorded a $3&nbsp;million loss on the sale and divestiture-related costs of $27&nbsp;million in 2017 and $84&nbsp;million in 2016. The company recorded these costs within cost of sales
and selling, general and administrative expenses of its Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;1, 2016, the company completed the sale of a confectionery
business in Costa Rica represented by a local brand. The company recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $9&nbsp;million in 2016. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;2, 2016, the
company purchased from Burton&#146;s Biscuit Company certain intangibles, which included the license to manufacture, market and sell Cadbury-branded biscuits in additional key markets around the world, including in the United Kingdom, France,
Ireland, North America and Saudi Arabia. On a constant currency basis, the purchase added incremental net revenues of $9&nbsp;million in the three months and $59&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisition integration costs </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within the
company&#146;s AMEA segment, in connection with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Vietnam, the company recorded integration costs of $1&nbsp;million in the three months and $3&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 and
$1&nbsp;million in the three months and $7&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016. The company recorded these acquisition integration costs in selling, general and administrative expenses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>2014-2018 Restructuring Program </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On May&nbsp;6,
2014, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a $3.5&nbsp;billion restructuring program and up to $2.2&nbsp;billion of capital expenditures. On August&nbsp;31, 2016, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a $600&nbsp;million
reallocation between restructuring program cash costs and capital expenditures so that now the $5.7&nbsp;billion program consists of approximately $4.1&nbsp;billion of restructuring program costs ($3.1&nbsp;billion cash costs and $1&nbsp;billion <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> costs) and up to $1.6&nbsp;billion of capital expenditures. The primary objective of the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and
overhead costs. The program is intended primarily to cover severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing-related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. Since inception, the company has incurred total restructuring and
related implementation charges of $3.3&nbsp;billion related to the 2014-2018 Restructuring Program. The company expects to incur the full $4.1&nbsp;billion of program charges by <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-end</FONT> 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring
charges of $117&nbsp;million in the three months and $535&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 and $234&nbsp;million in the three months and $714&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016 within asset impairment and exit
costs. These charges were for <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs are directly
attributable to restructuring activities; however, they do not qualify for special accounting treatment as exit or disposal activities. Implementation costs primarily relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection
with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the
company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $78&nbsp;million in the three months and $257&nbsp;million in the year ended December 31, 2017 and $86&nbsp;million in the three months and $372&nbsp;million in the
year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016. The company recorded these costs within cost of sales and general corporate expense within selling, general and administrative expenses. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain on equity method investment transactions </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On
October&nbsp;2, 2017, the company completed the sale of one of its equity method investments and received cash proceeds of $65&nbsp;million. The company recorded a gain of $40&nbsp;million within the gain on equity method investment transactions and
$15&nbsp;million of tax expense. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;3, 2016, a subsidiary of Acorn Holdings B.V. (&#147;AHBV&#148;) completed the $13.9&nbsp;billion
acquisition of all of the outstanding common stock of Keurig Green Mountain, Inc. (&#147;Keurig&#148;) through a merger transaction. On March&nbsp;7, 2016, the company exchanged with a subsidiary of AHBV a portion of the company&#146;s equity
interest in JDE with a carrying value of &#128;1.7&nbsp;billion (approximately $2.0&nbsp;billion as of March&nbsp;7, 2016) for an interest in Keurig with a fair value of $2.0&nbsp;billion based on the merger consideration per share for Keurig. The
company recorded the difference between the fair value of Keurig and its basis in JDE shares as a $43&nbsp;million gain on the equity method investment exchange in March 2016. Immediately following the exchange, the company&#146;s ownership interest
in JDE was 26.5% and its interest in Keurig was 24.2%. The company accounts for its investments in JDE and Keurig under the equity method and recognizes its share of their earnings within equity method investment earnings and its share of their
dividends within the company&#146;s cash flows. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">14 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee adjustments </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent
items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the third quarter of 2016,
the company began to exclude unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. To facilitate comparisons of its underlying operating results, the company has recast all historical <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures to exclude the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded net unrealized losses on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $27&nbsp;million in the three months and
$96&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 and $45&nbsp;million in the three months and $94&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company
recognized <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> losses of $97&nbsp;million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2016, within interest and other expense, net related to certain U.S. dollar interest rate swaps that the company no longer
designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to a change in financing plans. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;12, 2017, the company discharged $488&nbsp;million of its 6.500% U.S. dollar-denominated debt. The company paid $504&nbsp;million, representing
principal as well as past and future interest accruals from February 2017 through the August 2017 maturity date. The company recorded an $11&nbsp;million loss on debt extinguishment within interest expense. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;16, 2016, the company redeemed $850&nbsp;million of 2.250% fixed rate notes, maturing on February&nbsp;1, 2019, that were issued on
January&nbsp;16, 2014. The company recorded, within interest and other expense, net, a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> loss on debt extinguishment of $19&nbsp;million in connection with this redemption in the three months ended
December&nbsp;31, 2016. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October&nbsp;31, 2016, the company completed a cash tender offer and retired $3.18&nbsp;billion of its outstanding high coupon
long-term debt. The company recorded, within interest and other expense, net, a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses of $409&nbsp;million in the three months ended December&nbsp;31, 2016,
for the amount paid in excess of the carrying value of the debt and from recognizing in earnings the related unamortized discounts and deferred financing costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Intangible assets gains and losses </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Impairment
charges </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s annual testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible assets, the company recorded
$70&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2017 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than expected growth in part driven by decisions to redirect support from these trademarks to other regional and
global brands. The company recorded charges related to candy and gum trademarks of $52&nbsp;million in AMEA, $11&nbsp;million in Europe, $5&nbsp;million in Latin America and $2&nbsp;million in North America. In addition, during the third quarter of
2017, the company recorded a $1&nbsp;million impairment related to a transaction. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the second quarter of 2017, the company recorded a
$38&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge resulting from a category decline and lower than expected product growth related to a gum trademark in its North America segment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In the three months ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, during the company&#146;s annual testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT>
intangible assets, the company recorded $98&nbsp;million of impairment charges related to five trademarks. These charges related to biscuits, candy and gum trademarks of $41&nbsp;million in AMEA, $32&nbsp;million in North America, $22&nbsp;million
in Europe, and $2&nbsp;million in Latin America. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">15 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition, during the three months ended December&nbsp;31, 2016, the company recorded impairment charges of
$4&nbsp;million in AMEA and $4&nbsp;million in Europe related to biscuits trademarks. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2016, the company
discontinued one biscuit product that resulted in a $4&nbsp;million intangible asset impairment charge in its Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;30, 2016, in
connection with the company&#146;s global supply chain reinvention initiatives, the company made a determination to discontinue manufacturing a candy product that resulted in a $7&nbsp;million impairment charge in its North America segment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On March&nbsp;31, 2016, in connection with the sale of a confectionery business in France, the company recorded a $14&nbsp;million impairment charge for a
gum&nbsp;&amp; candy trademark as a portion of its carrying value would not be recoverable based on future cash flows expected under a planned license agreement with the buyer. In May 2016, the company recorded an additional $5&nbsp;million
impairment charge for a candy trademark to reduce the overall net assets to the estimated net sales proceeds after transaction costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Gain on sale of
an intangible asset </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On August&nbsp;26, 2016, the company recorded a $7&nbsp;million gain for the sale of a U.S.-owned biscuit trademark. The gain was
recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses of its North America segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On May&nbsp;2, 2016, the company completed the sale of certain
local biscuit brands in Finland as part of the company&#146;s strategic decisions to exit select small and local brands and shift investment toward its Power Brands. The sales price was &#128;14&nbsp;million ($16&nbsp;million as of May&nbsp;2, 2016)
and the company divested $8&nbsp;million of indefinite lived intangible assets and less than $1&nbsp;million of other assets. The company received cash proceeds of &#128;12&nbsp;million ($14&nbsp;million as of May&nbsp;2, 2016) and another
&#128;2&nbsp;million ($2&nbsp;million as of October&nbsp;31, 2016) following the completion of post-closing requirements. The additional $2&nbsp;million of consideration increased the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of
$6&nbsp;million recorded in the second quarter of 2016 to a total 2016 <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $8&nbsp;million. This transaction was recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses of the company&#146;s
Europe segment. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Incremental expenses related to the malware incident </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;27, 2017, a global malware incident impacted the company&#146;s business. The malware affected a significant portion of the company&#146;s global
sales, distribution and financial networks. In the last four days of the second quarter and during the third quarter, the company executed business continuity and contingency plans to contain the impact, minimize damages and restore its systems
environment. To date, the company has not found, nor does the company expect to find, any instances of Company or personal data released externally. The company has now restored its main operating systems and processes as well as enhanced its system
security. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During 2017, the company estimates that the loss of revenue as a result of the malware incident had a negative impact of 0.4% on its net
revenue and Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred incremental expenses as a result of the incident of $30&nbsp;million in the three months and $84&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 as part of the recovery effort.
The company also continues to make progress on its efforts to strengthen its security measures and mitigate cybersecurity risk. The company believes the recovery from this incident is largely resolved now and does not expect significant ongoing
impacts or incremental expenses from this incident on future periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Benefit from resolution of tax matters </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the fourth quarter of 2017, a U.S. federal court decided a customs case in the company&#146;s favor. As a result, the company released a Cadbury customs
tax reserve previously recorded as part of the Cadbury acquisition that was no longer required and recognized income of $7&nbsp;million within selling, general and administrative expenses in its North America segment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2017, the Brazilian Supreme Court (the &#147;Court&#148;) ruled against the Brazilian tax authorities in a leading case related to
the computation of certain indirect <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(non-income)</FONT> taxes. The Court ruled that the indirect tax base should not include a value-added tax known as &#147;ICMS&#148;. By removing the ICMS from the tax base, the
Court effectively eliminated a &#147;tax on a tax.&#148; The company&#146;s Brazilian subsidiary had received an injunction against making payments for the &#147;tax on a tax&#148; in 2008 and since that time until December 2016, the company had
accrued for this portion of the tax each quarter in the event that the tax was reaffirmed by the Brazilian courts. On September&nbsp;30, 2017, based on legal advice and the publication of the Court&#146;s decision related to this case, the company
determined that the likelihood that the increased tax base would be reinstated and assessed against the company was remote. Accordingly, the company reversed its accrual of 667&nbsp;million Brazilian reais, or $212&nbsp;million as of
September&nbsp;30, 2017, of which, $153&nbsp;million was recorded within selling, general and administrative expenses and $59&nbsp;million was recorded within interest and other expense, net. The Brazilian tax authority may appeal the Court&#146;s
decision, seeking potential clarification or adjustment of the terms of enforcement. The company continues to monitor developments in this matter and currently does not expect a material future impact on its financial statements. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">16 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">As part of the company&#146;s 2010 Cadbury acquisition, the company became the responsible party for tax matters
under a February&nbsp;2, 2006 dated Deed of Tax Covenant between the Cadbury Schweppes PLC and related entities (&#147;Schweppes&#148;) and Black Lion Beverages and related entities. The tax matters included an ongoing transfer pricing case with the
Spanish tax authorities related to the Schweppes businesses Cadbury divested prior to the company&#146;s acquisition of Cadbury. During the first quarter of 2017, the Spanish Supreme Court decided the case in the company&#146;s favor. As a result of
the final ruling, during the first quarter of 2017, the company recorded a favorable earnings impact of $46&nbsp;million in selling, general and administrative expenses and $12&nbsp;million in interest and other expense, net, for a total <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> impact of $58&nbsp;million due to the reversal of Cadbury-related accrued liabilities related to this matter. In the third quarter of 2017, the company recorded additional income of $3&nbsp;million related
to a bank guarantee release within selling, general and administrative expenses and interest and other expense, net. In the fourth quarter of 2017, the company recorded additional income of $1&nbsp;million related to a final bank guarantee release
within selling, general and administrative expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>CEO transition remuneration </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;20, 2017, Dirk Van de Put succeeded Irene Rosenfeld as CEO of Mondel&#275;z International in advance of her retirement at the end of March
2018. In order to incent Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put to join the company, the company provided him compensation with a total combined target value of $42.5&nbsp;million to make him whole for incentive awards he forfeited or grants that were not made to him
when he left his former employer. The compensation the company granted took the form of cash, deferred stock units, performance share units and stock options. In connection with Irene Rosenfeld&#146;s retirement, the company made her outstanding
grants of performance share units for the 2016-2018 and 2017-2019 performance cycles eligible for continued vesting and approved a $0.5&nbsp;million salary for her service as Chairman from January through March 2018. The company refers to these
elements of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s compensation arrangements together as &#147;CEO transition remuneration.&#148; The company is excluding amounts it expenses as CEO transition remuneration from its 2017 and future <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts are not part of the company&#146;s regular compensation program and are incremental to amounts the company would have incurred as ongoing CEO compensation. As a result, in
2017, the company excluded amounts expensed for the cash payment to Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put and partial vesting of his equity grants. In 2018, the company expects to exclude amounts paid for Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s service as Chairman and partial
vesting of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s equity grants. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>U.S. tax reform discrete impacts </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On December&nbsp;22, 2017, the United States enacted tax reform legislation that included a broad range of complex provisions impacting the taxation of
businesses. Some impacts of the new legislation would generally require accounting to be completed in the period of enactment, however in response to the complexities of this new legislation, the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission
(&#147;SEC&#148;) issued guidance to provide companies with relief. Specifically, when the initial accounting for items under the new legislation is incomplete, the guidance allows the company to include provisional amounts when reasonable estimates
can be made or to continue to apply the prior tax law if a reasonable estimate of the impact cannot be made. The SEC has provided up to a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-year</FONT> window for companies to finalize the accounting for the
impacts of this new legislation and the company anticipates finalizing its accounting during 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">While the company&#146;s accounting for the
legislation is not complete, the company has made reasonable estimates for some provisions and has recorded a $59&nbsp;million discrete net tax benefit in its 2017 financial statements. This net benefit is primarily comprised of a
$1,317&nbsp;million provisional charge for the estimated transition tax, offset by a $1,311&nbsp;million provisional deferred tax benefit from revaluing its net U.S. deferred tax liabilities to reflect the new U.S. corporate tax rate as well as an
additional $61&nbsp;million deferred tax benefit related to changes in the company&#146;s indefinite reinvestment assertion. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company
determines its constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the
comparable prior-year period to determine what the current period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">17 </P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company&#146;s outlook for 2018 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted Operating Income margin, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Adjusted Effective Tax Rate are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
that exclude or otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such as the impact of changes in foreign currency exchange rates, restructuring activities, acquisitions and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile
its full year 2018 projected Organic Net Revenue growth to its full year 2018 projected reported net revenue growth because the company is unable to predict the 2018 impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign
exchange rates, which could be material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2018 projected Adjusted Operating Income margin to its full year 2018 projected
reported operating income margin because the company is unable to predict the timing of its Restructuring Program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and
forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2018 projected Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its full year 2018
projected reported diluted EPS growth because the company is unable to predict the timing of its Restructuring Program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and
forecasted currency derivative contracts, impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures as well as the impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which could be material as a significant
portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its full year 2018 projected Adjusted Effective Tax Rate to its full year 2018 projected reported effective tax rate because the company is unable to
predict the timing of its Restructuring Program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency derivative contracts and impacts from potential
acquisitions or divestitures. Therefore, because of the uncertainty and variability of the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable
effort. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">18 </P>
